Thanks a lot for the reply, I will do that, I have given small kernel module which I feel this is the way of testing preemptiveness of the kernel.The below shown module I am using

#define __KERNEL__
#define MODULE
#include<linux/kernel.h>
#include<linux/module.h>
#include<linux/sched.h>


static int init_module(void)
{
unsigned long num=jiffies+(10*HZ);
while(jiffies!=num) {

? //schedule(); /* uncomment this line to relinquish the CPU*/
? ? ? ? }

return -1;
}

static void cleanup_module(void)
{
? ? ? ? printk("module unloaded\n");
}



When you try to load the above module since it is a non-preemptible kernel, it will in that loop for 10 secs(since it is jiffies+(10*HZ)).So during that U try type some thing OR try to move the mouse since it is non-premtible kernel you can't do anything.If it is a pr-emtible it will allow you to do so(This is what my way of testing if any comments OR better way of testing pls let me know).

"At a recent computer expo (COMDEX), Bill Gates reportedly compared the    
computer industry with the auto industry and stated,"If GM had kept up     
with the technology like the computer industry has, we would all be        
driving $25.00 cars that got 1,000 miles to the gallon."                   
                                                                           
In response to Bill's comments, General Motors issued a press release      
stating: If GM had developed technology like Microsoft, we would all be    
driving cars with the following characteristics:                           
                                                                           
1. For no reason whatsoever, your car would crash twice a day.             
                                                                           
2. Every time they repainted the lines in the road, you would have to buy  
a new car.                                                                 
                                                                           
3. Occasionally your car would die on the freeway for no reason. You would 
have to pull over to the side of the road, close all of the windows, shut  
off the car, restart it, and reopen the windows before you could continue. 
For some reason you would simply accept this.                              
                                                                           
4. Occasionally, executing a maneuver such as a left turn would cause your 
car to shut down and refuse to restart, in which case you would have to    
reinstall the engine.                                                      
                                                                           
5. Macintosh would make a car that was powered by the sun, was reliable,   
five times as fast and twice as easy to drive - but would run on only five 
percent of the roads.                                                      
                                                                           
6. The oil, water temperature, and alternator warning lights would all be  
replaced by a single "This Car Has Performed An Illegal Operation" Warning 
light.                                                                     
                                                                           
7. The airbag system would ask "Are you sure?" before deploying.           
                                                                           
8. Occasionally, for no reason whatsoever, your car would lock you out and 
refuse to let you in until you simultaneously lifted the door handle,      
turned the key and grabbed hold of the radio antenna.                      
                                                                           
9. Every time a new car was introduced car buyers would have to learn how  
to drive all over again, because none of the controls would operate in the 
same manner as the old car.                                                
                                                                           
10. You'd have to press the "Start" button to stop the car.

Subject: [Ilugc] apt doesn't resume after re-dialing to ISP
In-Reply-To: <8816fcf804081712403c803987@mail.gmail.com>
References: <8816fcf8040817091839be8f31@mail.gmail.com>	<20040817183926.GA1993@symonds.net>
	<8816fcf804081712403c803987@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <41229AB0.8060409@frodo.hserus.net>

Sridhar R wrote:

> The problem is automating this when the line automatically gets busy
> or down (eg. sancharnet.)

/etc/ppp/ip-up.local and /etc/ppp/ip-down.local (though debian does like 
renaming config files and changing their paths all over the place to fit 
them into debconf, which makes it a bit of a nuisance finding the right 
file to edit sometimes)

it's not a resume in that sense at all. If the process gets stopped if 
your internet connection just went away, you do have to download the 
package again with wget at least.

If you use an ftp mirror of debian, and an ftp client like lftp or ncftp 
you have a few more options - a lot of ftp servers can resume broken 
downloads better than http servers can.

	srs

Dear Friends,

It seems to be costlier connection when compared with BSNL. BSNL offers 
second telephone line for existing landline phone subscribers. This 
second line is dedicated only for Internet. You can use BSNL NetOne 
Accountless Internet package with this line.

No installation charges.
Monthly rental of Rs 499/- or Rs 399/- depends on your telephone 
exchange irrespective of usage.
Your NetOne charges will be extra at the rate of Rs 6 per hour of 
connection.
Unlimited download.
24 hours available. (i.e NO TIME LIMIT or BANDWIDTH LIMIT).
Download speed is 4 to 5 KB/Sec consistently. At worst case it is 2.5 
KB/Sec.

Regards
T.KaruppuSwamy

I don't think Sify is costlier than BSNL.

Justification:

Assuming you are online for 10 hours a day, your Netone charges will be 
INR. 1800 (300x6). Also you have to pay INR. 499 for the phone line 
which put together comes to INR. 2299 which is nearly four times the 
rate of Sify.

PS: If you assume that you are online for 24 hours a day, the amount is 
even more higher. Please correct me if I am wrong. Sridhar is using this 
connection. He can give a bigger picture on this.

From karthick.sundararajan at wipro.com  Wed Aug 18 11:03:44 2004
From: karthick.sundararajan at wipro.com (karthick.sundararajan@wipro.com)
Date: Wed Aug 18 11:03:54 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Sify Connection
Message-ID: <B99FECA7782B834AB0D4D5B18D89F5F00172BE96@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>


Hi,

	I enquired about the Sify Connection. These are the details that
I received:
1)	The Installation charges depend on the availability of some
other Sify customer in your neighbourhood. This means that if your
neighbour has it, then the charges are minimal. If no one in your area
has it, then "God save you".
2)	The monthly rental is Rs.600 for unlimited usage at 256Kbps/6 =
48.x Kbps. In other words, 256 Kbps is divided into a maximum of 6
users.

	Though the first point seems to suggest towards BSNL connection,
as the installation cost is lesser in BSNL, this is a one time cost and
can be overlooked when compared to the continuous cost incurred due to
telephone bills. Also the BSNL connection seems to be based on
telephones not cable connection. The latter is a better technology
(IMHO). So I prefer that.

	Rgds,
	Karthick S.
	Extn Number: 219
	CDC-1
	Wipro Technologies
	Chennai

Subject: Re: [Ilugc] Sify Connection


Dear Friends,

It seems to be costlier connection when compared with BSNL. BSNL offers
second telephone line for existing landline phone subscribers. This
second line is dedicated only for Internet. You can use BSNL NetOne
Accountless Internet package with this line.

No installation charges.
Monthly rental of Rs 499/- or Rs 399/- depends on your telephone
exchange irrespective of usage.
Your NetOne charges will be extra at the rate of Rs 6 per hour of
connection.
Unlimited download.
24 hours available. (i.e NO TIME LIMIT or BANDWIDTH LIMIT).
Download speed is 4 to 5 KB/Sec consistently. At worst case it is 2.5
KB/Sec.

Regards
T.KaruppuSwamy

monthly). Decent 24 hr connection considering just 600 rupees a

also. Even Today If I connect to Sify using RH9 I may not be able to browse.

Subject: [Ilugc] encrypted file system.

You can try cfs. 
<--
 Description: Cryptographic Filesystem
 CFS pushes encryption services into the Unix(tm) file system. It
 supports secure storage at the system level through a standard
 Unix file system interface to encrypted files. Users associate a
 cryptographic key with the directories they wish to protect.
 Files in these directories (as well as their pathname components)
 are transparently encrypted and decrypted with the specified key
 without further user intervention.
 -->

bsd unix wrote:
> Thanks for your replies.
> I concluded that the chipset used in the ZyAir has linux drivers based on a perticular web site 
> but it is not so.
> 
> Could you let me know whether your wireless adapter works with freebsd / linux or has drivers for it.
> If so could you tell me where it is available in chennai ?

According to some preliminary googling you might want to try the 
orinoco_cs drivers - its a prism 2.x / zcomax clone pcmcia rather than a 
pci card.

Alternatively if you have windows drivers for that card you can run them 
under linux using http://ndiswrapper.sourceforge.net

I'm connected to the net using a centrino ipw2200 inbuilt wlan card 
right now - using ndiswrapper and the windows drivers for the card.

From vkanakala at fastmail.fm  Wed Aug 18 16:16:48 2004
From: vkanakala at fastmail.fm (Vamsee Kanakala)
Date: Wed Aug 18 16:17:04 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: RSS Client
In-Reply-To: <cfvb61$hhg$1@sea.gmane.org>
References: <cfva0m$f5i$1@sea.gmane.org> <41232BCC.2080109@frodo.hserus.net>
	<cfvb61$hhg$1@sea.gmane.org>
Message-ID: <41233398.3060200@fastmail.fm>

This is not linux based, but I'll give you the simplest and best option: 
Bloglines.

http://www.bloglines.com

It is web-based, so you can read your subscriptions from everywhere, and 
the rate at which they add features and support for new formats (like 
Atom) is simply awesome. Try it once, and you'll be hooked. Plus, no 
irritating ads. If you use firefox, even better. There is a extension 
which easily allows you to sign up to a feed just with a mouse click. 
They even give you a email id, which lets you read email you can read 
from your bloglines account (isnt' that awesome? rss-enabled email!) and 
LOTS of other features. I have no idea how they make money out of this, 
but it simply *rocks*.

-Vamsee Kanakala.

Suraj Kumar <suraj@symonds.net> wrote:

> ,----
> | (Every morning I will see the updated system :-).

> I used to have 30 day uptimes  and such (only a powercut would stop my
> machine!). Shutdown your PC and give  it some rest...  or you will end
> up spoiling your CPU/memory (just like what I did :( )

Daily updates won't download more than 10 MB on average.  So within an
hour or so the computer will automatically shut down.

$ (apt-get update && apt-get -d dist-upgrade); echo -e "\a"; sleep 60;
echo -e "\a"; ./done

And when going to sleep, I will do ..

$ cat > ./done
/sbin/poweroff
$

(Morning)
$ apt-get dist-upgrade
$ # Fresh system!

  u can't hv connection directed to another system
using usb.

  downstream has to be a usb device(system writes)
  upstream from a usb device(system reads)

> 
> i guess u need to hv a seperate interface to do that 
> 
>   u can't hv connection directed to another system
> using usb.
> 
>   downstream has to be a usb device(system writes)
>   upstream from a usb device(system reads)
> 
> -shekar
> 
> 
> --- saravanan ganapathy <sarav_gsa@yahoo.com> wrote:
> 
> > Hai.
> >    I need to have a provision of filetransfer
> > between
> > linux machines using USB cable.
> >   Can you please help me to suggest the best way to
> > do
> > it? 
> > 
> > Sarav

This is possible.

You can connect two computers through their USB port using something
called an USB networking device. Once this is done, they can form an IP
network and any protocol build over IP can be used --- NFS, FTP, HTTP,
etc. 

HTH,
Suriya

  Apart from the earlier advice of upgrading the kernel,
I'd also add that you've chosen the wrong OS for this system.
FC2 is a desktop-oriented distro, not an enterprise server.
The bugs (and there are many) have not been worked out yet.
You'd be better off with RH Advanced Server 2.1 or Enterprise
Linux 3, or the free as in free lunch alternative: White
Box Enterprise Linux.

Subject: [Ilugc] Centrino on SuSE 9.1

Hi all,


	 I just got myself a Wipro LittleGenius CP laptop.

	Everything works fine, almost out of the box. Except the centrino. I am able 
to detect the card and stuff. Im unable to connect to an access point.

Here is what I did:

1. Installed SuSE 9.1
2. Downloaded and installed firmware from ipw2100.sf.net
3. Downloaded and compiled the module for the same.
4. Loaded the  module.
5. ipw2100 is detected.
6. YaST is started for configuring the IP and such. No DHCP here.
7. I do `dmesg` and I see 'Association lost'. Meaning that it connected and 
then was forced out due to WEP stuff.

Note: Im able to use the PCMCIA WLAN card and connect to the AP. 

Its a D-link AP and adapter pair that I am using right now for connectivity. I 
sincerely hope someone has setup centrino around here with WEP stuff.

Thanks in advance.

> to detect the card and stuff. Im unable to connect to an access point.

i think you'd have an ipw2200 centrino on most modern pentium M chipsets

i'd suggest that you use the ndiswrapper.sourceforge.net (free, gpl) or 
driverloader ($20 after 30 days free, www.linuxant.com) driver wrappers 
and install the windows drivers

It does wep too as far as I can see, and connects me at 802.11g (54 
Mbps) - the ipw drivers just do 802.11b

also install the wireless-tools rpm (though suse should have done that 
for you as you are associated using a pcmcia card .. stuff like iwconfig 
etc ...)

It'll detect the interface as wlan0 - so you might have to create a 
separate file setting for wlan0 like eth0 etc (like 
/etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/wlan0 in redhat - dunno what its in suse)

Note: the linuxant site has a link to a 16kstacks patch for 2.6 that 
you'll need for both ndiswrapper and linuxant - the centrino uses 12k of 
stack - you typically have upto 4k tops.

	srs

ps - this is typed on an acer travelmate 292 laptop running slackware 
10, kernel 2.6.8.1 with the 16kstacks patch, some ACPI patches ... 
[still got to configure ACPI properly on this one .. the laptop shipped 
with rh9 and a custom 2.4.20 kernel, that wasn't too much to my taste]

From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Fri Aug 20 14:43:54 2004
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Fri Aug 20 14:43:21 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Regarding Installing Debian
In-Reply-To: <OF6E229C68.93103528-ON65256EF6.003104ED-65256EF6.003104F1@notes.caritor.com>
References: <OF6E229C68.93103528-ON65256EF6.003104ED-65256EF6.003104F1@notes.caritor.com>
Message-ID: <4125C0D2.7030309@frodo.hserus.net>

Noorul Islam wrote:
> 
>   Is that possible to install a debian packages from internet through a
>   proxy server??
> 

Yes, definitely.

root:~# export HTTP_PROXY = http://your.proxy.server:proxy-port

Then if you have http mirrors in your apt.sources list, you will get apt 
to pull down these packages through your proxy server.

	srs

From kk_jay82 at yahoo.co.in  Fri Aug 20 02:18:45 2004
From: kk_jay82 at yahoo.co.in (Jayakumar KK)
Date: Fri Aug 20 14:48:56 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] 8139 realtek driver installation problem 
In-Reply-To: <20040820052231.67880.qmail@web53702.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20040820091845.99774.qmail@web8309.mail.in.yahoo.com>

HI
--Naveen S wrote:
> when i try to insmod realtek driver the following
> error i am getting plz suggest 
> 
> insmod -f 8139too.o
> 8139too.o: unresolved symbol synchronize_irq
> 8139too.o:

Seems there's a dependency failure i.e a lower level
module is needed so as to insmod this driver. Try
modprobe.

AFAK these network drivers need another low-level
module mii.o. so try insmoding mii.o first and then
8139too.o

> Hint: You are trying to load a module without a GPL
> compatible license
>       and it has unresolved symbols.  The module may
> be trying to access
>       GPLONLY symbols but the problem is more likely
> to be a coding or
>       user error.  Contact the module supplier for
> assistance, only they
>       can help you.
> 

More information on the kernel version and whether its
a kernel compiled by u or from a standard distribution
will help us in providing a detailed solution.

Jayakumar K K

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Sat Aug 21 05:57:51 2004

Subject: [Ilugc] Debian's new installer - A walkthrough.
In-Reply-To: <41245C37.8030309@frodo.hserus.net>
References: <4124419D.6080402@symonds.net> <41245C37.8030309@frodo.hserus.net>
Message-ID: <20040820195751.GA12710@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

Suresh Ramasubramanian wrote:
> Praveen wrote:
> >FYI, http://www.linuxbeta.com/slideshows/slideshow.php?release=59&slide=1
> 
> damn, the installation is starting to look more slackware-ish

Being an old debian hand, I find this installer annoying.  Too much
chatter.   The installer's job is to bootstrap your machine with a
self-sufficient stand-alone distro as easily as possible.  The second
stage installer 'base-config' can be as smart as it wants.

The potato installer was the best, as simple as a knife and fork.  All
you need to get the potato installer going was a kernel, a rootfs and
the live fs tarball.  You could easily get it going on extremely tricky
hardware - no fdd, cdrom, etc.

Infact installing potato was so easy that you did not even need the
installer!   Just untar the live fs tar ball into a dir and chroot.
Minor configuration and presto!  Instant potato installation inside a
chroot!

With potato even cross-installation was feasible. Say you had a Arm
board on which you needed to install potato.  You could untar the live
fs tar ball into a dir on your PC and nfs export it.  Then just boot the
Arm machine with an appropriate kernel and mount root over nfs.
That's it.

All this was possible because the first stage installer did a simple
job.  Woody was still manageable, but sarge looks bad.  Maybe with time
we'll get used to the beast.

> the last time i saw debian was years back .. dselect endless loop made 
> me rather allergic to it.

I'm sure you realise that you don't have to use dselect if you don't
like it.  Tasksel and apt can be run anytime later.

- Raja

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Sat Aug 21 17:01:43 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar B.)
Date: Sat Aug 21 17:02:10 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Urgent Help on Perl CGi
In-Reply-To: <20040821110108.88849.qmail@web40904.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20040821110108.88849.qmail@web40904.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <4127329F.5030905@chandrashekar.info>

prakash wrote:

> --------------apache error.log-------------------------------
> failed: FATAL:  IDENT authentication failed for user "user" at 
> /var/www/cgi-bin/select1.cgi line 6
> Can't call method "prepare" on an undefined value at 
> /var/www/cgi-bin/select1.cgi line 8.
> ----------------------------------------------------------

It seems that your postgresql database is configured for IDENT 
authentication scheme. In that case,  the UNIX user-id of the executing 
CGI script (apache webserver, apropriately) must be the same user as the 
postgres database user. I believe that this is not the case (CGI scripts 
normally run as user 'nobody' or 'apache' on most Linux distributions).

You might want to edit your pg_hba.conf file and change the 
authentication scheme for 'user1' from 'ident' to 'password' or 'crypt' 
scheme.

The URL http://www.faqs.org/docs/ppbook/c15679.htm has some good 
documentation on how to modify authentication scheme in your pg_hba.conf 
file.

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Sat Aug 21 22:55:10 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar B.)
Date: Sat Aug 21 22:55:27 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Boot problem
In-Reply-To: <32b5ee76040821085935c3cad9@mail.gmail.com>
References: <32b5ee76040821085935c3cad9@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <41278576.5030508@chandrashekar.info>

Varun Soundararajan wrote:

>now my prob is that when i boot to linux all i get is the grub
>loader.but when i try to find VMLinuz file to load the kernel (i
>gaveTabSpace to c the root dir files) but it is listing my E drive.so
>unable to boot to linux
>  
>
At the grub> prompt, maybe you must try the following sequence of commands:
--------------
   root (hd0,6)
   kernel /boot/vmlinuz
   boot
--------------
(hd0,6) is grub's way of accessing hda7.

/boot/vmlinuz must be replaced by the correct path to your linux kernel 
(using tab completion might help) in the above commands.

Once you boot successfully, you might want to create a menu.lst at the 
grub config location (generally, /boot/grub/menu.lst) with a menu of 
choices for your OS to boot. 

Let me know if you've had success with booting from the above commands.

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Sun Aug 22 10:06:52 2004
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy (T & B))
Date: Sun Aug 22 10:00:36 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Kernel upgrade problem 2.4.18-14 to latest 2.6.8.1 kernel
Message-ID: <412822E4.3090102@tandbintl.com>

Dear Friends,

I am in the process of upgrading my Redhat 8.0 kernel 2.4.18-14 to 
latest 2.6.8.1 kernel. All configuration, compilation, boot loader went 
through fine. The 2.6.8.1 kernel loaded successfully without any error. 
When the /etc/ rc.sysinit script is executed I have the problem of /proc 
filesystem error. Since in 2.6.8.1 kernel proc filesystem ( /proc ) has 
been replaced with sysfs (/sys), it is facing issues in finding the 
/sys/mount file and other files in /sys. Script is not able to run the 
fsck on mounted file system. I replaced all the reference to /proc file 
system in rc.sysinit with  /sys file system.

Can anybody help me on this?

Regards
T.KaruppuSwamy

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Sun Aug 22 11:10:06 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar B.)
Date: Sun Aug 22 11:10:18 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Kernel upgrade problem 2.4.18-14 to latest 2.6.8.1 kernel
In-Reply-To: <412822E4.3090102@tandbintl.com>
References: <412822E4.3090102@tandbintl.com>
Message-ID: <412831B6.8020108@chandrashekar.info>

T.KaruppuSwamy (T & B) wrote:

>  Since in 2.6.8.1 kernel proc filesystem ( /proc ) has been replaced 
> with sysfs (/sys), 

No. sysfs and procfs are two different things altogether. sysfs is a 
virtual filesystem like procfs, but it provides information only about 
hardware/devices of your system. procfs consists of various stuff 
exported by the kernel to the userland programs (which include process 
information, mount-points, memory-maps, module specific exported data , 
hardware information, networking subsystem, and so on).

> it is facing issues in finding the /sys/mount file and other files in 
> /sys. Script is not able to run the fsck on mounted file system. I 
> replaced all the reference to /proc file system in rc.sysinit with  
> /sys file system.

You must enable procfs support in your kernel configuration and 
recompile it. No changes to sysinit scripts are necessary. Additionaly, 
to mount sysfs during boot time, you must add the following line into 
your /etc/fstab:
     none   /sys   sysfs   defaults   0   0

Also, make sure that the procfs entry remains in your /etc/fstab.

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

Sivasankar Chander wrote:

>>When the /etc/ rc.sysinit script is executed I have the problem of /proc 
>>filesystem error. Since in 2.6.8.1 kernel proc filesystem ( /proc ) has 
>>been replaced with sysfs (/sys), it is facing issues in finding the 
>>/sys/mount file and other files in /sys. Script is not able to run the 
>>fsck on mounted file system. I replaced all the reference to /proc file 
>>system in rc.sysinit with  /sys file system.

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Sun Aug 22 11:38:50 2004
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy (T & B))
Date: Sun Aug 22 11:32:30 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Kernel upgrade problem 2.4.18-14 to latest 2.6.8.1 kernel
In-Reply-To: <412831B6.8020108@chandrashekar.info>
References: <412822E4.3090102@tandbintl.com>
	<412831B6.8020108@chandrashekar.info>
Message-ID: <41283872.1070300@tandbintl.com>

Dear Chandrashekat,

Thanks for explaining the difference between proc and sysfs. I will 
compile with proc support and revert back

Regards
T.KaruppuSwamy

Chandrashekar B. wrote:

> T.KaruppuSwamy (T & B) wrote:
>
>>  Since in 2.6.8.1 kernel proc filesystem ( /proc ) has been replaced 
>> with sysfs (/sys), 
>
>
> No. sysfs and procfs are two different things altogether. sysfs is a 
> virtual filesystem like procfs, but it provides information only about 
> hardware/devices of your system. procfs consists of various stuff 
> exported by the kernel to the userland programs (which include process 
> information, mount-points, memory-maps, module specific exported data 
> , hardware information, networking subsystem, and so on).
>
>> it is facing issues in finding the /sys/mount file and other files in 
>> /sys. Script is not able to run the fsck on mounted file system. I 
>> replaced all the reference to /proc file system in rc.sysinit with  
>> /sys file system.
>
>
> You must enable procfs support in your kernel configuration and 
> recompile it. No changes to sysinit scripts are necessary. 
> Additionaly, to mount sysfs during boot time, you must add the 
> following line into your /etc/fstab:
>     none   /sys   sysfs   defaults   0   0
>
> Also, make sure that the procfs entry remains in your /etc/fstab.
>
> Cheers,
> Chandrashekar Babu.
>
>
>

Very true. I wonder how many among us are really comfortable

point for our dominance in IT.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Sun Aug 22 20:07:29 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sun Aug 22 20:26:52 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Kernel upgrade problem
In-Reply-To: <41289F15.3030404@frodo.hserus.net>
Message-ID: <20040822143729.282E71B3F5@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> # Lots of stuff compiled into the kernel (no harm done but I prefer 
> modular kernels)
> 
  I prefer to compile in some critical stuff, including netfilter, SCSI,
ethernet drivers, some filesystems, crypto, etc. (both for performance
as well as enhanced immunity from rootkits that modify /lib/modules/...).

> # No hotplug enabled (but why?)
> 
  Probably overlooked - I'm not currently using any USB or PCMCIA device.

> # OSS instead of ALSA sound drivers
> 
  Some Ogle and Xine binaries which were precompiled and configured for
OSS - I'll eventually get around to rebuilding them for ALSA.

-Siva

wouldn't have had such complex hardware interfaces and applications that 
abstract them like we see today.  In my opinion, our first successful 
application would be natural language processor for our native languages 
- A computer with just a talking device and a listening perhaps. One 
that understands the language we speak, and simply reply back in our 
native language. Most indian languages have a high degree of 
predictability in terms of grammar, syllable, flow and pronounciation,

simply communicates with us verbally, and listens to us. Life would've 
been a lot simpler.

productive, efficient, less error-prone and *most important* - use our 
creativity and common sense (which the computers even today lack) like 
our predecessors (before 3000 years) did.

Dear Linuxians,

/etc/fstab as you said... ( as a newbie i am amazing with the .config 
file... it is really helpful to customize our own kernel.. what i have 
understood is right?)

At the stage of "make install" i am getting the following error message:
"No module /bin/true found for kernel 2.6.8.1"
and make install failured! As per my understanding /bin/true is a binary 
executable file which returns true while executed... it is not a 
module... then how come this message?

/etc/modules.conf file. How to get it back or generate? :( :(

Please help me to track down the issue?

Regards
T.KaruppuSwamy


Chandrashekar B. wrote:

> T.KaruppuSwamy (T & B) wrote:
>
>>  Since in 2.6.8.1 kernel proc filesystem ( /proc ) has been replaced 
>> with sysfs (/sys), 
>
>
> No. sysfs and procfs are two different things altogether. sysfs is a 
> virtual filesystem like procfs, but it provides information only about 
> hardware/devices of your system. procfs consists of various stuff 
> exported by the kernel to the userland programs (which include process 
> information, mount-points, memory-maps, module specific exported data 
> , hardware information, networking subsystem, and so on).
>
>> it is facing issues in finding the /sys/mount file and other files in 
>> /sys. Script is not able to run the fsck on mounted file system. I 
>> replaced all the reference to /proc file system in rc.sysinit with  
>> /sys file system.
>
>
> You must enable procfs support in your kernel configuration and 
> recompile it. No changes to sysinit scripts are necessary. 
> Additionaly, to mount sysfs during boot time, you must add the 
> following line into your /etc/fstab:
>     none   /sys   sysfs   defaults   0   0
>
> Also, make sure that the procfs entry remains in your /etc/fstab.
>
> Cheers,
> Chandrashekar Babu.
>
>
>

T.KaruppuSwamy (T & B) wrote:
> At the stage of "make install" i am getting the following error message:
> "No module /bin/true found for kernel 2.6.8.1"
> and make install failured! As per my understanding /bin/true is a binary 
> executable file which returns true while executed... it is not a 
> module... then how come this message?

Did you upgrade modutils (and the other stuff required before you can 
upgrade from 2.4 to 2.6) first?

> For your kind info: In the process of debugging this problem, i lost my 
> /etc/modules.conf file. How to get it back or generate? :( :(

2.6.x uses /etc/modprobe.conf and this is generated by running

# /sbin/generate-modprobe.conf > /etc/modprobe.conf

	srs

Ananth G wrote:

>hi all,
>   I have fedora core 2 installed my system , and i'd like to try out
>slackware 9, and install them both on the same disk and share the /home
>partition and swap(if possible i'd like to share  /boot , can i share
>anything else) .
>I like to do this bcoz ,this is interesting. i will be creating the
>users & groups with same ids in both the OSes. what are the changes
>that i have to make,
>what are the problems that i may encounter ,and things to keep in mind
>before doing
>this . 
>  
>
Make sure that you dont share / and /usr and /var partitions.  [assuming 
that / partition hosts the directories /etc, /lib, /sbin directories]. 
Sharing the same users and groups could mean sharing a common /etc 
directory... which in my opinion can raise other complicated issues 
[imagine having to manage a common sysinit scripts for both your distros!].

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

Date: Mon Aug 23 12:43:29 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] boot  -reg
In-Reply-To: <B99FECA7782B834AB0D4D5B18D89F5F00172C8F1@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>
References: <B99FECA7782B834AB0D4D5B18D89F5F00172C8F1@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>
Message-ID: <41299945.202@frodo.hserus.net>

karthick.sundararajan@wipro.com wrote:
> Hi,
>  
>     I am a "been there-done that" guy for you. Here are the steps that I 
> followed:
>  
> 1) Install Win98 (A minimal installation would do)
> 2) Install Win2k in a separate drive.
> 3) Install RH9.0 after this (ofcourse on a separate Logical drive)
> 4) **************Do Not Overwrite Win98 **********************

you actually dont need to do that .. you can boot into your linux root 
partition from a cd if your master boot record gets overwritten after 
windows got installed

and for this guy - he's already got a working dual boot box and wants to 
boot into linux by default instead of windows

for that - edit /etc/lilo.conf (or /etc/grub.conf) and check the default 
boot there.

in lilo you'd just modify default=linux to default=winxp (assuming the 
two entries are labeled linux and winxp), then run lilo (/sbin/lilo -v)

in grub - the OS's to be booted are listed in order - 0,1,2,3 etc (0 is 
the first one is 0 and then on. Change the default=0 (or whatever) in 
there to the appropriate number for the windows partition. Once the 
grub.conf is modified you dont need to run anything, unlike in lilo

>  
> Rgds,
> Karthick S.
>

Date: Mon Aug 23 12:57:01 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] boot  -reg
In-Reply-To: <B99FECA7782B834AB0D4D5B18D89F5F00172C91A@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>
References: <B99FECA7782B834AB0D4D5B18D89F5F00172C91A@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>
Message-ID: <41299C6F.3020607@frodo.hserus.net>

karthick.sundararajan@wipro.com wrote:

> Would that mean booting with a CD always? I am not aware of this method.
> Can you please explain?

boot in with a cd the first time. once you have booted in, run lilo or 
grub again

when you boot in with a redhat / slackware cd etc - you get a boot: 
prompt.  You can either hit enter to boot straight from the cd, or you 
can do this:

boot:  linux root=/dev/hda1 noinitrd ro

assuming the kernel on that redhat cd is called "linux" .. in slackware, 
it'd be called "bare.i" so you'd enter bare.i root= etc

that'll put the overwritten mbr back in place

alternatively, you could create a linux boot floppy using the boot 
images on the rh cd and the rawrite / rawritewin.exe tool and do this 
using the boot floppy

	srs
From tom at tharayil.com  Mon Aug 23 02:43:16 2004
From: tom at tharayil.com (Tom Jose Tharayil)
Date: Mon Aug 23 13:00:12 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] boot  -reg
In-Reply-To: <B99FECA7782B834AB0D4D5B18D89F5F00172C91A@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>
References: <B99FECA7782B834AB0D4D5B18D89F5F00172C91A@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>
Message-ID: <51677.192.76.54.23.1093246996.squirrel@www.tharayil.com>

 ----------------------------------
>
> Would that mean booting with a CD always? I am not aware of this method.
> Can you please explain?
>
of course not !
As Srs neatly explained you would have to boot into your machine and
tailor the boot loader be it lilo or grub.
Subsequently install grub/lilo on the MBR by running grub-install /dev/hda
or /sbin/lilo and then when the machine boots
you would be presented with the loader.
The poster was saying that the default option was on windows.
SRs gave the method to change that option to Linux.
After the timeout exceeds it would boot into Linux by default

What are the advantages of such a method ?
===========================================
* you are working remotely and you might have to reboot the system from
the remote location several times, and if it is a dual boot system then it
has to boot into Linux. By ensuring that the default option is Linux, this
is possible.


--

Tom Jose Tharayil
tom@tharayil.com

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Mon Aug 23 13:03:18 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar B.)
Date: Mon Aug 23 13:03:56 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Sharing patitions between linux distributions
In-Reply-To: <79b11cb804082300162e782033@mail.gmail.com>
References: <79b11cb80408162342707dfe3b@mail.gmail.com>	<79b11cb804082223256ddac11b@mail.gmail.com>	<412992E2.1020306@chandrashekar.info>
	<79b11cb804082300162e782033@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <41299DBE.5040405@chandrashekar.info>


Ananth G wrote:

>can the sysinit scripts be shared? why not , if it cant be shared, can
>u pls tell me why, 
>
As long as you know in detail what your sysinit scripts do and tweak 
them to suit your need to boot both Fedora, as well as Slackware. There 
are lots of other configuration files which are different in both these 
distros. For example, apache configuration files vary (Fedora uses 
Apache2, Slackware uses Apache 1.3.x). The default user/group scheme are 
different across these distributions. Some programs in Slackware behave 
a little differently than the similar counter-parts in Fedora.

Simply put, there's a lot of work involved in ironing out the oddities 
of both the distro, sharing the same config files. I guess the more 
effort you put into it... you will either end up converting slackware to 
resemble redhat, or vice-versa (sysinit, configuration, libraries, so 
on). You might end up losing the very essence of either distributions 
(system startup, default configuration, and so on).

But it can be fun way of learning how one distro is different from the 
other (as long as you dont end up losing valuable data).

Good luck with it :-)
Chandrashekar Babu.

Manikanda Prabhu wrote:

You can use a BNC(bouncer) service or get a ssh tunnel to some outside host.

karthick.sundararajan@wipro.com wrote:

>
>	Can you please tell me the services that I can run/I should not
>run. That is the grey area for me.
>
>  
>
As a rule, run only those services that you require to be running for 
your work. You might also want to run certain services *only* when 
required (xinetd comes to my mind, for example). Not only does this save 
memory and reduce the boot/shutdown time, but also makes your system a 
bit secure.

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Tue Aug 24 21:25:41 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar B.)
Date: Tue Aug 24 21:25:59 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] installing wxWindows-2.4.2
In-Reply-To: <1093358247.3085.148.camel@localhost.localdomain>
References: <1093358247.3085.148.camel@localhost.localdomain>
Message-ID: <412B64FD.2050708@chandrashekar.info>

ashwin kesavan iyengar wrote:

>that i have to run ldconfig. When i did, it returned command not found.
>Though man ldconfig does exists. Further it says to modify
>LD_LIBRARY_PATH ( or equivalent) environment variable. How do i modify
>it & what do i modify in it. Any help in this regard would b a great
>  
>
Seems to me, that you tried running 'ldconfig' as a normal user. If that 
was the case, you should be running it as '/sbin/ldconfig' (as /sbin is 
generally not in the default PATH for normal users). However, you are 
advised to run '/sbin/ldconfig' as root.

You can temporarily sort out this issue, by adding the path to your 
wxwindows library into your LD_LIBRARY_PATH environment variable. 
Assuming that the wxwindows library was installed in /usr/local/lib,
you might try 'export LD_LIBRARY_PATH=$LD_LIBRARY_PATH:/usr/local/lib/'  
at your bash prompt. I'm not sure if wxwindows creates a subdirectory 
under /usr/local/lib and stores its libraries in there. If that is the 
case, you must want to modify the path appropriately.

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Wed Aug 25 10:05:52 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar B.)
Date: Wed Aug 25 10:06:08 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] /dev/tty and /dev/fd0
In-Reply-To: <20040825025416.53506.qmail@web11411.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20040825025416.53506.qmail@web11411.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <412C1728.1090706@chandrashekar.info>

babu jayapaul wrote:

>dear friends,
>
>I compiled new kernel 2.6.8. in fedora core 2. there
>is no /dev/fd0 and /dev/ttyx, in ctl+atl+F2 GUI is
>running. how can I create this fd0 device and virtual
>consoles. please help me
>  
>
Regarding the /dev/ttyx, you must've disable "Virtual Terminal Support" 
in your kernel configuration. Make sure that you have these entry under 
the character devices in your .config file (created in the 
/usr/src/linux/ directory):
 
  CONFIG_VT=y
  CONFIG_VT_CONSOLE=y
  CONFIG_HW_CONSOLE=y

Optionally, you can set the option while running the 'make menuconfig' 
under the "Device Drivers"->"Character Devices"->"Virtual Terminal". 
Also enable "Support for console on virtual terminal" setting.

Regarding the /dev/fd0, you must enable "Normal floppy disk support" 
under "Device Drivers"->"Block devices" section (either as module, or as 
kernel builtin).

Let us know if this helped!

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

also schedule update on other Linux distros by setting up a cron job 
appropriately. Most  "enterprise-friendly" distros do have a tool 
similar to up2date.

of the earlier mechanism :-)

From metallica_tony at yahoo.com  Wed Aug 25 07:27:57 2004
From: metallica_tony at yahoo.com (Sriram K)
Date: Wed Aug 25 19:58:04 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Creating RPMS
Message-ID: <20040825142757.90295.qmail@web51907.mail.yahoo.com>

Put ur gzipped or bzipped tar file in /usr/src/redhat/SOURCES directory. Create a spec file and place it in /usr/src/redhat/SPECS directory. From there u execute 
rpmbuild -ba <spec file name>.spec
After completion, u can get ur rpms and srpms from /usr/src/redhat/RPMS and /usr/src/redhat/SRPMS directories respectively. U can create ur own basic spec file easily, after having a look at "maximum-rpm", a book for rpm packagers. Include only the essential entries in the spec file. Its not needed that u shud include all available options.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Wed Aug 25 19:43:15 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Wed Aug 25 20:02:48 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] How to create RPM file?
In-Reply-To: <20040825131149.36841.qmail@web8509.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20040825141315.D8FAE1B3F5@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> I am having source code tar file for a project.
> I am having patch file for that project.
> 
> How to create RPM file for that tar with patch?
> 
  The patch utility does not create RPM files; it just makes changes
to your source tree based on the patchfile.

  RPM files are created using the rpm and rpmbuild family of
utilities. These perform their function under control of various
configuration files, and most importantly, a file called the 'specfile'
that controls how the source is rebuilt, installed, uninstalled, etc.

  Some Open-Source projects include a generic specfile that is usable
for creating an RPM for some common distributions (RedHat, Mandrake, SuSE,
etc.). To create an RPM from a tarball when the specfile is already in
the tarball, do:

rpmbuild -ta <package>.tar.gz

  If the specfile is not present in the tarball, the above step will
fail. You'll then need to write a specfile, details of which are
documented in the RPM-HOWTO.

  In some cases, you may have to modify the generic specfile to make
it function correctly for your distribution.

-Siva

ashwin kesavan iyengar wrote:

>It seems that doing a su != logging as root. 
>Thank you once agian.
>
>  
>
Just a note: Doing an 'su -' as normal user should be almost like 
logging in as root. Doing an 'su' alone will switch your privilege level 
to root, but wont run root's startup profile scripts (thus, PATH and 
various other root specific settings aren't updated).

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

Date: Thu Aug 26 12:50:10 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] best one  among squid,iptables-masqurade,route
In-Reply-To: <20040826062712.82937.qmail@web11411.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20040826062712.82937.qmail@web11411.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20040826072004.GB7190@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

babu jayapaul wrote:
> I have to share my internet to a small network of 100
> in my campus, I have a confusion how to share my net
> by squid proxy or iptables or routing the packets.
> which one  is better regarding the spead.

Squid is a better tool for sharing web (http/ftp) access.  Squid +
Squidguard will give you plenty of control - you can authenticate users,
monitor and filter web access to your hearts content.

Use iptables for other access - mail, ssh, etc.

- Raja

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Aug 26 03:07:50 2004
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Aug 26 15:37:59 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Error in awk script
In-Reply-To: <B99FECA7782B834AB0D4D5B18D89F5F00177A6A9@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>
Message-ID: <20040826100750.93267.qmail@web50208.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi!
 
> My awk code was:
> $ awk ' { if ( length($0) > 80 ) { printf $FILENAME,
> $NR, "\n"} } ' *.c
> >>/tmp/code

Try this:

#!/bin/bash
#Script: len.sh
#Pass the directory as an argument to script
if [$# -ne 1]; then
  echo "Usage: len [directory]"
  exit 1
fi
for file in `ls $1`; do
  awk 'length($0) > 80 {print FILENAME, NR, $0, "\n"}'
$file
done

I will really encourage you to go through some online
awk tutorials:

An AWK Tutorial:
http://www.vectorsite.net/tsawk.html

AWK Tutorial:
http://stud.wsi.edu.pl/~robert/awk/

Guided tour of awk:
http://www.vectorsite.net/tsawk1.html

Regards,

Shaks

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Fri Aug 27 10:05:53 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar B.)
Date: Fri Aug 27 10:06:09 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] share traffic with 2 cards : urgent help
In-Reply-To: <20040827033921.91632.qmail@web11401.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20040827033921.91632.qmail@web11401.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <412EBA29.3030603@chandrashekar.info>

babu jayapaul wrote:

>my problem:
>
>when i use 'iptraf' to moniter the traffic i found all
>the traffics/requests goes to eth2 and not to eth1 and
>eth1 is free with no traffic.
>
>I want to share the request/traffic with both the
>cards or any alternet way please help me.
>
>  
>
A quick (though non-optimal solution to work-around this issue would be 
as described below:
 1. Create an ethernet bridge interface (say, br0) and assign an IP 
address for the same.
2. Add both eth1 and eth2 to the bridge
3. Set the default route to the bridge interface.

You might need to install 'bridge-utils' to manage ethernet bridges 
(available at http://bridge.sourceforge.net). There's a howto document 
available at http://bridge.sourceforge.net/howto.html - which might help 
you in configuration/commands.

Note: Above configuration should setup both your ethernet interfaces to 
the same IP address - thus allowing all requests/traffic to be shared. 

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

> Dear Friends
> 
> I have 2 public ips for internet and i also configured both 
> ips using 2 eth device, both are working fine in my fedora 
> core2 system and i am used the following command to redirect 
> and share the net
> 
> iptables -t nat -A POSTROUTIMG -o eth1 -j MASQUERADE
> 
> iptables -t nat -A POSTROUTIMG -o eth2 -j MASQUERADE
> 
> my problem:
> 
> when i use 'iptraf' to moniter the traffic i found all the 
> traffics/requests goes to eth2 and not to eth1 and
> eth1 is free with no traffic.
> 
> I want to share the request/traffic with both the cards or 
> any alternet way please help me.
> 
> thanks in advance

Your default route must be pointing to eth1. Setup a multipath default route
and do not use equalise (packet based) for this will break your NAT. Since
you are using masquerade, I assume your Publix IPs are not static. In that
case, you will need to fire up the multipath commad in the interface up
script.

Warm regards
Mohan

Desktop or laptop, we could have the same problem. In desktops, you have the
luxury of sticking in cards which is not feasible in notebooks. If you are
just developing with a fixed set of interface devices which are available in
the laptop, both are identical. IMHO, desktops are more flexible for this
purpose. I know people who use notebooks for developemnt and a old desktop
like a PII/PIII for testing/ deployment where all cards are plugged in -
thus giving portability and ability to test well.

Warm regards
Mohan

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Fri Aug 27 21:05:46 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar B.)
Date: Fri Aug 27 21:05:57 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] linux partition-reg
In-Reply-To: <20040827140317.8607.qmail@web8505.mail.in.yahoo.com>
References: <20040827140317.8607.qmail@web8505.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <412F54D2.9010404@chandrashekar.info>

j. manikandan wrote:

> Dear Friends,
>  
> During Partition of linux i given the var partition less in my server 
> . It is possible to add more space to var partition from other 
> partitions like home the home partition has additional space.
> Please guide me to solve this issue.
> regards
> j.manikandan.
>  
> File system looks like this.
> Filesystem           1K-blocks   Used     Available  Use% Mounted on
> /dev/hda2              1510060    138700   1294652  10%   /
> /dev/hda1               497829     13283    458844   3%     /boot
> /dev/hda3              1004052    128952    824096  14%  /home
> none                     62364         0           62364     0%   /dev/shm
> /dev/hda7             10175300   4663232  4995180  49% /usr
> /dev/hda6               497829    438191     33936     93%   /var 

If you had configured lvm while partitioning your hard disk,  the issue 
could've been sorted out in a simpler way.

Anyways, a crude way of solving this issue would be as below:
1. Run a 'du -sk /var/*' and make a note of directories which take up 
more space.

2. Make a recursive copy of those directories (use 'cp -a' to be safe) 
into a mouted partition with more space (for e.g. /usr).

3. Once you've confirmed that the files are safely copied (with 
attributes, permissions intact), delete the original directories (the 
ones in /var) that you copied. [You can directly use the 'mv' command 
and move those directories, but I would be a little hesitant to do such 
a thing on a live machine].

4. Create symbolic links from /var to the newly copied (or moved) 
directories ('ln -s').

[Boot from a linux rescue CD-ROM and mount these partitions in 
directories under /mnt or similar locations, to be more safe (to avoid 
problems with lock files). Change directory path indicated above 
appropriately.]

 From now on, files that get created in some directories of /var will be 
stored in /usr (or other partition where you linked the directories).

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

hello,

I have small problem in dns 
before we got network 10.2.0.0/255.255.0.0
and the named.conf file is like this 
##############################################################
zone "fire.org" {
        type master;
        file "fire.org";
        allow-transfer { 10.2.1.32; 10.2.1.34; 10.2.1.35; };
};
zone "rrg.fire.org" {
        type master;
        file "rrg.fire.org";
        allow-transfer { 10.2.1.32; 10.2.1.34; 10.2.1.35; };
};
zone "2.10.in-addr.arpa" {
        type master;
        file "10.2.reverse";
        allow-transfer { 10.2.1.32; 10.2.1.34; 10.2.1.35; };
};
##################################################################
it is working fine with old network.
but now we have implemented vlan on network like,
vlan1 10.200.1.0
vlan2 10.201.1.0
vlan3 10.202.1.0
vlan3 10.2.1.0
now vlan3 ip's r working fine because they r in 10.2.1.0 network
but,i want to add some hosts which r on 10.200.1.0,10.201.1.0 network 
how ?

what changes should i do on my dns server so, that all my vlan's hosts
can resolve.

venu
the doublethumb .........
-- 
  T.K.Venu Gopal
  v27076685@fastmail.fm

    step 1:[upgrading kernel]
    This problem persists in both kernels-2.6.5-1.358 and 2.6.6-1.427.
    I have sent the /var/log/message in fedora core 2.
    step 2:[change modem init strings in kppp and wvdial]
    While searching i found that replacing correct modem init scripts 
rectifies the problem.
    I found the respective inf file in windows xp and copied the init 
strings.
    These are the modem init strings in my windows *.inf  file.I 
replaced the modem init string in /etc/wvdial.conf and ran wvdial as root.
    HKR,  Init,          1,, "AT<cr>"
    HKR,  Init,          2,, "AT&FE0V1S0=0&C1&D2+MR=2;+DR=1;+ER=1<cr>"

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Fri Aug 27 23:20:06 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar B.)

Subject: [Ilugc] re: xandros installation problem
In-Reply-To: <412F2279.6070303@eth.net>
References: <412F2279.6070303@eth.net>
Message-ID: <412F744E.8060904@chandrashekar.info>

boovarahan s wrote:

> Hi  All !
>
> When I install Xandros , it probes the hardware but after some time 
> the screen goes blank and the system hangs.
>
> How to correct it ?
>
It seems to me that your video card is not well supported by Xandros. A 
temporary work-around would be to hold the shift key, as soon as you see 
the Xandros logo during bootup. You will provided with a series of 
choices for booting. Select "VESA Mode" in the menu of choices (using 
your arrow keys) and continue booting.

If it boots, expect a slow performance and occasional display corruption 
while using your desktop environment. If the problem still persists, 
then it might be due to some other hardware that Xandros failed while 
initializing.

In my experience, Xandros is tightly integrated with very little room 
for customizability (unlike other linux distros - 
SuSE/Mandrake/Knoppix). Trying to disable hardware probe (which can be a 
little difficult though), might result in boot failure.

This distro is well suited for absolute non-technical end-users who wish 
to migrate from Windows and own branded (familiar models) computers. But 
not recommended for experienced or even intermediate users who'll want 
flexibility or customizability. If it doesn't support your hardware, 
there's nothing much you could do about it (unless of course, you 
"bought" an Official copy of Xandros which carries a support license 
with it).

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From Toufeeq_Hussain at infosys.com  Sat Aug 28 20:38:58 2004
From: Toufeeq_Hussain at infosys.com (Toufeeq Hussain)
Date: Sat Aug 28 20:42:31 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] processor's  across network.
Message-ID: <2616BDAAA87AAD44A649D877241FB8A3068FD7@hydmsg04.ad.infosys.com>


The Answer your looking for:

OPEN MOSIX

www.openmosix.org

>From the Sourceforge page, here's an excerpt

What is openMosix?
openMosix is a Linux kernel extension for single-system image clustering.  This kernel extension turns a network of ordinary computers into a supercomputer for Linux applications.

Once you have installed openMosix, the nodes in the cluster start talking to one another and the cluster adapts itself to the workload. Processes originating from any one node, if that node is too busy compared to others, can migrate to any other node. openMosix continuously attempts to optimize the resource allocation.

We achieve this with a kernel patch for Linux, creating a reliable, fast and cost-efficient SSI clustering platform that is linearly scalable and adaptive. With openMosix' Auto Discovery, a new node can be added while the cluster is running and the cluster will automatically begin to use the new resources.

There is no need to program applications specifically for openMosix. Since all openMosix extensions are inside the kernel, every Linux application automatically and transparently benefits from the distributed computing concept of openMosix. The cluster behaves much as does a Symmetric Multi-Processor, but this solution scales to well over a thousand nodes which can themselves be SMPs.

The openMosix Community is very active, contributing add-on applications and sharing helpful information with all users.  The openMosix Add-Ons and Community page lists these shared applications.  And, it is all GPL'd.

Regards,
TH
From siva at dias.ath.cx  Sat Aug 28 20:46:19 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sat Aug 28 21:06:07 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] processor's  across network.
In-Reply-To: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420A3BCB10@ccr.satyam.com>
Message-ID: <20040828151619.735E11B405@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
>   I have 2 systems at home .. one a p3 700 mhz 512 mb ram working fine . and
> the second one p2 
> 
> In other words I want machine 1 to be integerated with machine 2. which will
> give me dual processor machine.
> 
  If you get hold of a motherboard that is SMP-capable (examples
are the Intel 440FX/LX/BX and the Serverworks LE/HE), you can get another
PIII 700 and put together a dual-CPU SMP machine with two PIIIs. 

  The reason that this is not even worth the effort, is that a single
Tualatin Celeron 1.4 GHz can comfortably outperform this combination,
and only costs about Rs.2000 (CPU only).

  It isn't really worth trying to get any additional power out of what
you already have, since there are far cheaper single-processor alternatives
out there.

  If you want to go faster, an AMD Athlon 64/2800 is about 4 times as
fast and only costs about Rs.13k (Mobo + CPU). An AMD Opteron 240
dual-CPU configuration is only Rs.45k (motherboard + 2 CPUs) and is about
6 times as fast.

> Is it possible to somehow say to machine 1 that there is another processor
> avilable in machine 2 which should be taken as integeral part of the system

  Clustering - either Mosix or Beowulf, but in all cases a two-node cluster
is next to worthless because of communication overheads. The clustering
SW also has to be locally installed or remote-booted through the network.

> 
> Machine 1 -must assume machine 2's processor as its second  processor. is it
> possible to achive this change thru some  kernel changes  or how do we go
> abt such a thing ?
> 
  It can't be done except as outlined above.

  You can consider converting your old PII to a thin-client setup running
LTSP or VNC or something similar, but it will still require a monitor
and a working boot device (either Etherboot/PXE or a floppy drive).

  Economically, I'd suggest harvesting the old machine for parts and selling
what you don't need. Use the proceeds to get a faster CPU for your present
machine. A 1.1 GHz Coppermine Celeron is a direct replacement for a PIII 700,
and should give you a nice 40% speed boost for < Rs.3k. As an added bonus,
you can recover cash by selling the PIII 700 as well, which can sometimes
fetch more money than a Celeron 1.1 GHz.

-Siva

From mksarav at gmail.com  Sun Aug 29 02:02:25 2004
From: mksarav at gmail.com (Saravanan M K)
Date: Sun Aug 29 14:32:34 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Google Gmail Review
In-Reply-To: <e2f046c0408290154234235fa@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e2f046c040829015154de92b4@mail.gmail.com>
	<e2f046c0408290154234235fa@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <e2f046c040829020239103d24@mail.gmail.com>

Dear All,

Some of you are already using Google Gmail (under beta testing).
Here is my first hand experience with it.

GMail Review

Ever since Google Gmail beta testing started, some of my friends got a
invitation and created their Gmail account. After using them for a
while, they inturn got invitation to invite other friends. Some of
them asked me whether I want one. I was keep on refusing since already
I have enough email accounts including my own personal email account
mks at mksarav dot org. However the curiosity to test Gmail features
was increasing day by day. Finally one day, suddenly I saw an
invitation waiting in my inbox sent by my B.Sc. classmate Durairaj who
is working for Cisco, Bangalore.

I accepted it and created an account-- mksarav at gmail dot com. As it
is with Google, Gmail user interface is also very simple. No popup ads
or anything like that during login till logout. After using it for 2
days I was quite impressed by its features especially key board
shortcut. I got a feeling like I am using PINE/Mutt as far as the
keyboard shortcut navigations are concerned. Because of it, the amount
of mails you can handle in a given amount of time is really high.

The user interface is based on Javascript with cookies enabled. As of
now, it will run on the following browsers:

Microsoft IE 5.5 and newer (Windows)
Netscape 7.1 and newer (Windows, Macintosh, Linux)
Mozilla 1.4 and newer (Windows, Macintosh, Linux)
Mozilla Firefox 0.8 and newer (Windows, Macintosh, Linux)
Safari 1.2.1 and newer (Macintosh)

However I tried it with only IE6.x and Mozilla 1.6. The UI is really
fast and I love the auto address completion from your contact list,
when you type email address in the {To, Cc, Bcc} fields. Atleast this
is the first time I am seeing such a feature in a web based email. So
just by touching a few key stroke, address is complete!

One of the important feature is "Conversation view". By default all
the emails are threaded and each conversation (thread) will look like
a deck of cards neatly arranged. I have used threading facility before
with many email clients. However, this is the first time I am seeing
such a wonderful interface. You will appreciate it if you use lot of
mailing lists.

And of course, it much spoken 1GB storage space must be known to
everyone by now.

There is no concept of "Folders" in Gmail (the same concept is also
there in Opera M2 mail client). Everything is stored under "All Mail"
including the sent mail. Whenever you want to retrieve a particular
mail, just type some keyword in the "Search Mail" box, voila -- your
mails are there! Whoever used Google there is no need to tell how
accurate it search results are, and especially in this case, the
search are limited to your mail box and hence more accurate results.

Instead of folders, Gmail uses a concept called "Label" (Opera M2
client calls it "View"). For e.g., I created several labels one for
each mailing list like -- slugnet, ilugc, linux-bangalore-programming,
etc., When you are reading any conversation from that mailing list,
just assign appropriate label to it by clicking a button. The entire
conversation will be marked with that label. Any new mails under the
same conversation will be automatically visible under that label. A
single conversation can be categorized under multiple label.

As of now, Gmail has some restrictions in what you can send/receive:

* The maximum size of the outgoing mail should be 10MB.

* For security reasons, any kind of executable files are not allowed
in the attachment. Meaning, .exe files are not allowed as attachment
even if it hides inside zip, tar.gz., tgz, .gz etc. In such a case,
the mail won't be sent or bounced to the sender. Since most of the
viruses spread as executable files, this measure will try to reduce
the spread of email viruses through Gmail.

One nice feature I liked is, when you send a mail to a mailing list,
usually you will also receive a copy of it. However in Gmail, you
won't receive it since it is already stored in "Sent Mail". It don't
want to clutter your mail box with multiple copies of the same mail.
If you are able to see your sent mail, then it is successfully
delivered to the mailing list. If not, obviously you will receive a
"Mail delivery notification for failed delivery". However, if you send
a mail for just yourself (i.e. you are the only recipient), then it
will be delivered.

Spam marking is there. It reminds me spam marking in Mozilla Thunderbird.
The feature I liked most is it keyboard shortcut like:

c for compose
/ for search
k move to new conversation
j move to older conversation
p move to previous message in a conversation
n move to next message in a conversation
o to open the message/conversation (from the index page)
u return to inbox or conversation list
r reply
a reply all
f forward
TAB+Enter to send the message
! mark a message as spam
and some more. For a detailed list check:
http://gmail.google.com/support/bin/answer.py?answer=6594&topic=-1

You will really appreciate the power of keyboard shortcut once you
start using it.

It comes with a nice spell checker also.

Overall I am feeling like it is directly working on my desktop rather
than web based since it is so fast.

Gmail by default uses Unicode UTF-8 encoding and hence you can cut and
paste the UTF-8 encoded text. For e.g., to send UTF-8 encoded Tamil
text, I open notepad in WinXP and type in Tamil using "Tavultesoft
Keyman" keyboard driver (with Unicode Tamil keyboard matrix file with
"Anjal" Tamil input method) and just cut and paste.

Since Gmail is still doing a beta testing to improve the features and
fix any bugs, it is not open to the public yet. i.e. You can't go to
http://gmail.google.com and create a account for you. Only some body
who are already using Gmail can invite you to create an account. Based
on availability of new storage space and other resources, Gmail is
allotting few invitations (say 5) to the existing Gmail users so that
they can invite their friends who will be interested in beta testing.
If you ever get any invitation, by all means accept it, and enjoy the
great Gmail features.

This review is also available at my diary:
http://www.mksarav.org/blog/blog.html

-- mks --

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Sun Aug 29 19:28:51 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Sun Aug 29 19:28:00 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Rockwell modem driver
References: <1093763431.2120.9.camel@localhost.localdomain>
Message-ID: <cone.1093787931.809454.20072.1000@mynx>

ashwin kesavan iyengar writes:

>    Before i switched over to linux(RH9) i was using windows 98SE. I find
> that the that my internet connection is much slower than it was under
> windows. 

Most issues with internet connectivity speed on Linux are due to improper 
configuration. On newer Redhat Linux (8.0/9.0/Fedora), the issue could be
a general performance decline due to the desktop bloat (Gnome does not 
perform well on machines with less than 256 MB RAM).

> I suspect it may b due to modem driver b'cos the modem driver's
> name is generic modem. I think a driver designed for this modem could
> deliver better performance.

Technically speaking, external (serial port) modems do not require drivers 
for functioning. However, you might have to modify the AT command set (for 
modem initialization) to vendor settings.


> I am using a Rockwell 56Kbps(Data/fax/voice)
> external modem. It would b helpfull if somebody could provide me with
> suggestion on how go abt. or link to the driver.

You can check these commands from Windows (in Control 
panel->Modems->Properties), and copy the same in your linux ppp 
dialer configuration (wvdial.conf, or KPPP, etc). 

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Mon Aug 30 10:01:47 2004
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy (T & B))
Date: Mon Aug 30 09:55:12 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Kernel upgrade successful! 
Message-ID: <4132ADB3.9030202@tandbintl.com>

Thanks my dear friends, for your support! I have successfully upgraded 
my kernel from 2.4.18.X to 2.6.8.1. it is working fine, i can feel some 
good improvement in speed also.. ( is it so, or is it to my blind 
eye?... :)  :) )

After long struggling as a newbie, At last i followed a simple method 
which made my job easy. i.e
1. copy the 2.4.18.X's .config file to 2.6.8.1's root directory (THIS 
STRATEGY HELPED ME TO SOLVE THE DEVICE DRIVER LOADING ISSUES FOR MOST OF 
THE HARDWARES - Here only I had got stuck up previously!!!!)
2. run "make menuconfig" on copied .config and add a additional features 
or missing features carefully.
3. Then "make bzImage; make modules; make modules_install; make install".
4. If you don't use grub,  make an entry for new kernel in 
/etc/lilo.conf and run "lilo"

Hope it may be useful for others also.

Thanks,
Regards
T.KaruppuSwamy

I doubt it, becuase Yahoo itself continues to bear with YahooPOPs!
(http://yahoopops.sourceforge.net/) which let's you *receive & send*
mails thru your regular mail client. It's effectively bypassing Yahoo's
advertising, ergo, Yahoo is losing atleast some amount of ad revenue.
But still, the project continues to thrive.

In the same way, Google is bearing with many apps like Gmail Notifier
extension for Firefox, and even recently released it's own version of
Gmail Notifier. Bottomline is that, they don't want to antagonize users
by disabling neat apps. You cand *depend* on M$ to do that, for sure ;)

-Vamsee Kanakala.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Aug 30 11:20:16 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Aug 30 11:40:13 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Rockwell modem driver
In-Reply-To: <20040830053701.A57AE4160A1@ws5-2.us4.outblaze.com>
Message-ID: <20040830055016.6028332BCD@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

[ Charset ISO-8859-1 unsupported, converting... ]
> >    Before i switched over to linux(RH9) i was using windows 98SE. I find
> > that the that my internet connection is much slower than it was under
> > windows.
> 
> This is a general problem which i also faced.

  I don't about RH 9, as I don't use it much. However, I've never had
a problem maxing out my DIAS connection on downloads on my RH7.3 system.
(And previously, I've used multi-Mbps broadband connections on RH73
notebooks with full bandwidth. Not to mention that I have no problems
maxxing out an 800 Mbps 4-port Tulip full-duplex fast Ethernet card
while doing LAN file transfers and the like). 

  56kbps is so slow that it looks like background noise to the networking
stack of the Linux kernel.

  The obvious things to look for are your modem initialization strings
that allow it to connect at maximum speed of your modem.

> I feel it is not a driver issue, but the way the data is transferred to the browser under X.

  This is nonsense, as anybody who uses Mozilla with kde/X can attest.

> I felt that All GUI stuff including refreshing is slower in linux than in windows.
> 
  Again, nonsense. GUI performance is one of the areas where XFree86 was always
way ahead of the Windows world, on well-supported hardware.

 You must be using a graphics card without decent XAA support under X
(probably a no-name SiS card or similar from China). SiS and various other
Asian manufacturers don not release programming information for their
chips in a timely manner - so there aren't any good open-source drivers
for their cards. If you've got one of those, tough luck. You're probably
stuck using X on the raw framebuffer.

  I'd suggest upgrading to halfway decent hardware (ATI, Matrox, NVidia,
Intel i810, i815 or similar, from good hardware companies with a track record
of open-source driver support) with XAA support in X, and see it fly.  It's
much faster than IE/Windows on exactly the same hardware. Even a lowly
S3 Trio or an Alliance AT3D PCI card (both of which sold for
~$2 or Rs.90 retail at Fry's way back in 1998) had scorching performance even
on a lowly 486/Pentium classic running XFree86 3.3.6. OTOH, a crappy
SiS63xx might well be over 100 times slower, even on a P4 3.06 GHz. YMMV -
there's no substitute for using your brains and doing some research before
obtaining HW.

-Siva

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Mon Aug 30 12:01:44 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Mon Aug 30 12:00:54 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Rockwell modem driver
References: <20040830053701.A57AE4160A1@ws5-2.us4.outblaze.com>
Message-ID: <cone.1093847504.856249.326.1000@mynx>


bsd unix writes:

> This is a general problem which i also faced.
> I feel it is not a driver issue, but the way the data is transferred to the browser under X.
> In other words i feel it is an issue with the x server and client.
> 
> I felt that All GUI stuff including refreshing is slower in linux than in windows.

Nope. As I quoted before, it can be a configuration issue. Moreover, this 
issue could be more tied down to supposedly "user-friendly" distros like 
RH/Fedora on their default autodetected configuration. If your system is 
slow/irresponsive, here are some quick hints to speed up:
1. Disable all startup services that you dont require. If possible, tweak 
around and optimize.

2. Check if your X Window System is configured to use the correct display
drivers [there are chances that your X display driver is set to VESA 
Framebuffer, which will definitely make your GUI too slow]. Where possible,
install the vendor supplied drivers for your display (eg., Nvidia cards, ATI
cards).

3. If your system has less memory (< 256 MB), switch to lean desktop
environments like XFCE, WindowMaker, IceWM, Enlightenment, or any other
window manager + file-manager of your choice.

4. Try moving to lean browsers like Firefox or Opera (as opposed to Galeon, 
Mozilla, Netscape and so on... they seem to be too slow at times).

5. If you are looking for good performance (at the cost of having to get 
your hands more dirty with manual configuration stuff), try Slackware (okay, 
you can also try Debian or Gentoo).

<rant>
Personally, I found Linux way much faster (than Windows 9x/2000 atleast) on 
my good old Thinkpad (which has 32 MB RAM). I use Openbox+ROX+Opera on 
this box, and its highly usable for web browsing atleast. Windows 2000 wont
even bother to start on this machine ;-).
</rant>

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Aug 30 11:44:04 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Aug 30 12:04:02 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Patch to allow postfix-1.1.12 to build cleanly with db4
Message-ID: <20040830061404.C72CB32BCD@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

Hi folks,
         I'm including a small patch to allow building postfix-1.1.12
(the last postfix1 release) to build cleanly on distros with Berkeley
db4, including RH8, 9, FC1, FC2, etc. If anybody out there still uses
Postfix1, give it a whirl. I'm using it in conjuction with Cyrus-SASL
1.5.28. It will probably also work on other postfix-1.1.x releases,
maybe with a line number offset - YMMV. I used it to patch postfix-
1.1.12-5.src.rpm (Google for this one).

##################### Begin postfix-dict_db.patch ####################
--- postfix-1.1.12/src/util/dict_db.c	Sun Aug 29 19:56:04 2004
+++ postfix-1.1.12-patched/src/util/dict_db.c	Sun Aug 29 19:57:21 2004
@@ -520,7 +520,7 @@
 	msg_fatal("set DB cache size %d: %m", DICT_DB_CACHE_SIZE);
     if (type == DB_HASH && db->set_h_nelem(db, DICT_DB_NELM) != 0)
 	msg_fatal("set DB hash element count %d: %m", DICT_DB_NELM);
-    if ((errno = db->open(db, db_path, 0, type, db_flags, 0644)) != 0)
+    if ((errno = db->open(db, NULL, db_path, 0, type, db_flags, 0644)) != 0) 
 	msg_fatal("open database %s: %m", db_path);
     if ((errno = db->fd(db, &dbfd)) != 0)
 	msg_fatal("get database file descriptor: %m");
###################### End postfix-dict_db.patch #####################

The main benefit of using Postfix1 is that there's a greater body of
knowledge of its quirks and oddities, so those who already have it
running well would prefer to continue using it. This patch allows that,
even on more recent distros.

-Siva

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Mon Aug 30 13:22:02 2004

Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Cone

Sivasankar Chander writes:

>   Pretty hilarious coincidence! I'm a CLI e-mail junkie myself (still
> on elm), so could you summarize some of the features/benefits of cone
> vis-a-vis elm/pine?

I landed up on Cone, on my quest to find a text-mode 'e-mail client' which 
can do the following:

1. Directly interact with my ISP's SMTP server (I can't burden my laptop 
with sendmail, exim, postfix, and so on).

2. Have inbuilt support for POP3/IMAP protocols (so I dont have to 
configure/run fetchmail) and built-in *sane* editor/composer.

3. Provide me a highly-usable interface, with least learning curve. I 
gave up on mutt for its complex configuration scheme, bizarre 
keyboard-shortcuts (of course, its configurable), and way too many features 
than I can handle, and a not-so-intuitive UI. I'm sure 'mutt-freaks' will 
want to flame me on this one ;-)

>From the usability point of view, cone's interface somewhat resembles pine, 
but it seems to be a superset of pine, in terms of features.

I hardly used elm, but I found it remind me of lynx web browser (I use 
'links' for web browsing).

I'm still figuring out certain things on Cone (need to find out how to 
configure threaded message display and so on).

In terms of resource usage, its a little bulky when compared to 
mutt/pine/elm (using up 4.9 MB on my box). But I guess its a compromise
for not having to run MTA and fetchmail on my machine.

You can check http://www.courier-mta.org/cone/index.html for more 
information and also downloads of cone. 

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Aug 30 13:22:32 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Aug 30 13:42:35 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Difference between distros
In-Reply-To: <79b11cb8040830002456b3432b@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20040830075232.02F0932BD9@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

>    I work on fedora core 2. but i still dont know what makes it
> special from other versions of GNU/Linux. I know that most of you
> use different distros. Could you tell me the difference between each
> distro i.e. the sysinit scripts, the tools that provides etc(specific diffs).
> 
  Apples and Oranges - there isn't anything special about any distro. 
It's just a matter of convenience, and there isn't a best distro that's
suitable for all people.

  Having said that, you can broadly divide distros into 2 main categories:
Source-based and Binary-based. Source-based distros (like Debian & Gentoo)
are more suitable for experienced Linux users who know what they're doing,
and binary-based distros (like Slackware, RedHat, Mandrake, Suse, etc.) are
more suitable for people who don't want to spend time rebuilding
stuff from scratch, and would rather install everything at one shot and
get on with it.

  Among the binary-based distros, you can divide them on the basis of the
kind of package-management system used (RPM or other). 

> GNU/Linux is the same but may be we can have a conversation and decide
> the best among them , not the best GNU/Linux but the best distribution.

  Well, as I said earlier, there isn't a single best distro. For me,
RedHat 7.3 has worked out very well as an excellent desktop as well as
server distro. With some difficulty, I've been able to keep it upgraded
and patched for a lot of the stuff (kernels, libraries, compilers, tools,
ABIs, APIs, apps, etc.) that were not even around when it first came out. 

  For most developers, RedHat 6.2 worked out even better with its bulletproof
glibc-2.1.3/egcs-1.1.2 combination.

  Both are rock stable, very versatile and quite fast, especially with
upgrades to more recent kernels. To me, the toolchain has to be
bulletproof (i.e. able to correctly build whatever is thrown at it without
patchwork on the tools themselves). That is not yet the case with the
bleeding-edge distros, since most of the gcc-3.x compilers still miscompile
a lot of existing code, including the 2.6.x kernel and some versions of
glibc.

-Siva

Suraj wrote:
> I see...  Me too  wants something similar.  I depend heavily  on mutt,

you have a symonds account right? so you can do something like this -

$ ssh -2 -L2525:localhost:25 suraj@puggy.symonds.net

in a separate terminal

Then in pine at least, point your smtp server to localhost:2525

In mutt, configure exim to use localhost:2525 as the smtp server (google 
for exim ssh tunnel and you'll find a howto with the appropriate config)

  Thanks - this could be a good alternative for my setup. Configuring
elm and fetchmail is very easy, but the MTA (postfix + cyrus-sasl in
my case) is always tricky. My setup is also a dyndns.org setup with
postfix, cyrus-sasl, ddclient on my desktop/server, which sits on
an internal LAN behind a separate, standalone linux NAT/firewall/router
that connects to the WAN. Any change in my WAN transport layer (such as
a shift to another ISP or DSL service) is isolated to the linux router.

  The original intent behind going with postfix was that I'd eventually
move the MTA portions into the firewall, leaving only the mail clients 
on the other machines. But that idea is faulty, since the firewall is always
on and susceptible to power surges and so on. So it can't run a full-
featured distro, but only a minimal read-only root distro. That rules out
postfix and just about any other MTA on the firewall.

Also, I can replicate a firewall easily (it's a minimal router distro),
but MTA bring-up is hairy - so it's better left on my main desktop/server
machine.

Cone promises to be a reasonable alternative to the difficulties of 
maintaining an MTA on the desktop machine, as this is a critical point
of failure.

-Siva
