From mssnlayam at vsnl.net  Mon Aug 30 04:02:29 2004
From: mssnlayam at vsnl.net (Suriya Narayanan M S)
Date: Mon Aug 30 14:32:41 2004
Subject: Using Debian was (Re: [Ilugc] Difference between distros ,
	and the best distro?)
In-Reply-To: <3779a1e704083000394535fc3d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <79b11cb8040830002456b3432b@mail.gmail.com>
	<3779a1e704083000394535fc3d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20040830090229.GA28143@cs.utexas.edu>

On Mon, Aug 30, 2004 at 01:09:19PM +0530, Mohan Raj wrote:
> there must be some better way to install/maintain the sytem hardware/software.
> so what is it guys?

I use Debian unstable and I am really comfortable with it. Here are a
few things I would like to share.

1. Software maintenance is done by apt. I neither use dselect nor
tasksel. These are the commands I usually use --- apt-cache search,
apt-get install, apt-get update, apt-get upgrade.

You need to know a few things for example, install the package
x-window-system to install X, install the package kde for KDE, etc.

2. Install the package discover and it takes care of all hardware. You
need to answer a few simple questions for writing your /etc/X11/XF86Config-4

3. Know that only one application can write to /dev/dsp. I use KDE all
the time so have apps (mplayer, xmms, xine, mpg123, ogg123, etc. Though
I use only mplayer) writing to artsd. Some apps don't know to write to
artsd, in such a case instruct artsd to relinquish control over /dev/dsp
in maybe 3 seconds (can be done in KDE control center).

4. If you think a package needs to be configured, run "dpkg-reconfigure
PACKAGE"

HTH
Suriya

> 
> IMO gcc-3.x is a bloatware of a compiler suite. It took me around 16 hours 
> to compile the 2.2.26 kernel on my Thinkpad (Pentium 133) using gcc-3.2.3. 
> The same compiled within 5 hours while using gcc-2.96 - and I fail to 
> understand an acceptable reason for this.
> 
Seems a little excessive, so I suspect insufficient memory, with 
thrashing. I haven't actually tried gcc-3.2.3 extensively, but I can
state that the gcc-3.3.3 compiler seems to work better. It has
good forward & backward correctness (it can compile newer as well as
relatively older code), and in most cases generates more efficient code
than gcc-2.96-110 (or whatever came with RH7.3), with similar compile
times (important for stuff like glibc and XFree86). Most build breakages
have been syntax related, but the compiler has actually uncovered
semantic errors that escaped with warnings on gcc-2.96 (like the patch
for postfix1 I posted today). So I think it is a step forward, even if
it uses more resources and occasionally miscompiles code, including
the kernel. 

Compiling the 2.6.8.1 kernel with it was a breeze - it was really quick
on a PIII/1 GHz/256 MB (say about 15 minutes with about a couple of dozen
modules).

On a P133 Thinkpad (similar to one I've got), I'd recommend staying with
egcs-1.1.2, although it rules out building some newer packages.

-Siva

-----Original Message-----
From: ilugc-bounces@ae.iitm.ac.in [mailto:ilugc-bounces@ae.iitm.ac.in] On
Behalf Of Toufeeq Hussain
Sent: Saturday, August 28, 2004 8:39 PM
To: ilugc@aero.iitm.ernet.in
Subject: RE: [Ilugc] processor's across network.



The Answer your looking for:

OPEN MOSIX

www.openmosix.org

>From the Sourceforge page, here's an excerpt

What is openMosix?
openMosix is a Linux kernel extension for single-system image clustering.
This kernel extension turns a network of ordinary computers into a
supercomputer for Linux applications.

Once you have installed openMosix, the nodes in the cluster start talking to
one another and the cluster adapts itself to the workload. Processes
originating from any one node, if that node is too busy compared to others,
can migrate to any other node. openMosix continuously attempts to optimize
the resource allocation.

We achieve this with a kernel patch for Linux, creating a reliable, fast and
cost-efficient SSI clustering platform that is linearly scalable and
adaptive. With openMosix' Auto Discovery, a new node can be added while the
cluster is running and the cluster will automatically begin to use the new
resources.

There is no need to program applications specifically for openMosix. Since
all openMosix extensions are inside the kernel, every Linux application
automatically and transparently benefits from the distributed computing
concept of openMosix. The cluster behaves much as does a Symmetric
Multi-Processor, but this solution scales to well over a thousand nodes
which can themselves be SMPs.

The openMosix Community is very active, contributing add-on applications and
sharing helpful information with all users.  The openMosix Add-Ons and
Community page lists these shared applications.  And, it is all GPL'd.

Regards,
TH

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Aug 30 17:05:03 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Aug 30 17:25:06 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] processor's  across network.
In-Reply-To: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420BBD7283@ccr.satyam.com>
Message-ID: <20040830113503.69E0D32BEA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> We have  a small program to find largest prime ( No threading etc etc )
> simple C program to find the largest prime (upto 18 digits). 
> 
> When I run only one instance of my program How do I make  it run in both the
> CPU's. 
> 
  There isn't any magic bullet to take a single thread of control in an
imperative programming language (like any common programming language
in widespread use - C, C++, Java, Pascal, VB ...)  and split it
into two threads of control automatically. It just isn't possible - basic
introduction to computers CS 001 (See footnote below).

 You'll have to program your
code as two threads using pthreads or fork(). Mosix will be able to move
your processes across CPUs, but I'm not sure about threads - they're 
probably bound to the CPU that runs the parent process.

 Also remember that there's a huge cost to moving an entire process
context from one system to another over the network.

> 
>  Assume we run SAP on a Linux (p4 3.4 GHz 2 2GB Ram) Lets say a BOM process
> runs for X hours . Now I upgrade it to a dual CPU machine will it still run
> for X hr or X/2 hrs ???

  If it's programmed as a single-process application, X hours + some overhead
for the SMP synchronization (say 1.1 X hours).

  If it's programmed as a dual-process application with perfect
synchronization, zero communication between processes, and perfect 
parallelization, about 0.5 X hours. In the real world, this isn't possible,
so you can expect anywhere between 0.5 X to 1000 X (the 1000 X comes from
pathological cases where one processor is practically idle,  waiting for
a result from the 2nd processor; the process is blocked and it's paged
out, until it gets a little piece of data from the 2nd processor and then
gets paged in for another small bit of computation before getting
blocked again, and so on. The costs of page faults, context switches, etc.
in these cases are huge).

  The short answer is that it depends on the nature of the computation
and the skill of the programmer. There are computations that are
intrinsically serial, i.e. cannot be parallelized at all, and there are
some algorithms that can be perfectly parallelized. 

Regardless of all this, Mosix, Beowulf or any other tool for that 
matter, can't do any magic that turns a
single-threaded application into a multithreaded one.

Footnote: 

However, there is an entirely different style of programming, called
Declarative programming, with functional-programming languages like FP, ML,
Prolog, pure LISP (not common LISP), where there is no abstract concept of a
thread of control. These can indeed be automatically parallelized.

The most widely-used declarative programming language is a hardware
simulation language called Verilog. Verilog simulation models can be
indeed be automatically parallelized, and there are numerous companies
that sell special systems that do just this (Ikos, Cadence/Quickturn,
Aptix/Mentor Graphics, etc.), in some cases with over a billion-times
speed-up over the software simulation. 

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Aug 30 17:19:50 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Aug 30 17:39:50 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] processor's  across network.
In-Reply-To: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420BBD728D@ccr.satyam.com>
Message-ID: <20040830114950.B300432BEA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
>   Thanks for ur mail.. My intention was just to use the cpu's for academic
> intrest. 
> I know very well that both my machines are outdated..
> 
  No, you don't get it - your systems aren't outdated until they're
no longer able to perform the task they're doing now.

  The issue of hooking up CPUs for getting additional processing
power, even from a purely academic perspective, is critically dependent
on the task which is sought to be performed, and is completely unrelated
to whether your system is outdated or not. Ceteris Paribus, a uniprocessor
solution is the only general-purpose solution that can run all applications
about equally well.

  There isn't any magic bullet that will generate parallelism where
none exists - this is the same blunder that caused CDAC to waste thousands
of crores of public money on a dead-end line of research into MPPs
over the last 15 years.

-Siva 
From Toufeeq_Hussain at infosys.com  Mon Aug 30 17:38:13 2004

>

> When I run only one instance of my program How do I make  it 
> run in both the

> Running in all the available CPU is what is desirable. 

This is where lam and mpi can help you  out.
LAM-MPI is Local Area Multicomputer, Message passing Interface.

check out www.lam-mpi.org
has the tutorial on how to setup and some sample code.

A brief explanation:

Say I have 2 nodes. node1 and node2.
My MPI-C Program is programmed in such a way that primes between 1 to 100 are calculated on node1 and primes between 100 to 200 are calculated on node 2.
both the results are then sent to node1.

MPI Programming is very simple and one can easily MPI-ize their existing C programs.
Good Code Reuseability.

Also another option is MPICH which enable you to also use Windows based machines in your cluster.

Another option is JAVA-RMI, a java implementation of mpi in java does exist.try google/linux

NOTE:: The above mentioned are for a Beowulf Cluster and I'm not sure if a MOSIX enabled system can successfully implement LAM-MPI.

Toufeeq Hussain
From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Aug 30 17:47:12 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Aug 30 18:07:14 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] processor's  across network.
In-Reply-To: <2616BDAAA87AAD44A649D877241FB8A3068FE9@hydmsg04.ad.infosys.com>
Message-ID: <20040830121712.9C4C832BED@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> > your processes across CPUs, but I'm not sure about threads - they're 
> > probably bound to the CPU that runs the parent process.
> > 
> 
> Are'nt just kernel threads processor bound?
> Think userland threads can be processor migrated...
>
  On a single system-image platform (like most SMP machines or NUMA
machines like the SGI Altix), I see no difficulty in migrating
threads (userland or kernel) across processors. That's because the
process context resides in memory and is equally accessible to any
thread regardless of the CPU it's running on.

  However, on a cluster like Beowulf or Mosix, the entire process
context has to be replicated in each node running a thread from this
process, and all copies have to be kept in synchronization over the
network (there is no shared memory). This is bound to be so expensive as
to make it completely impractical to migrate threads alone. A single
process context can be a multi-megabyte image.

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Aug 30 18:03:46 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Aug 30 18:23:45 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] processor's  across network.
In-Reply-To: <2616BDAAA87AAD44A649D877241FB8A3068FEB@hydmsg04.ad.infosys.com>
Message-ID: <20040830123346.90CF032BED@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> Don't we have an implementation of shared memory across processors on a Beowulf?
>
  It's possible to create a shared memory abstraction that uses underlying
network primitives to maintain synchronization, but it's only an simulation.
The actual implementation will be about seven orders of magnitude slower
as compared to a real shared-memory SMP machine.

  In simpler terms, Beowulf clusters don't share memory physically across
nodes, but the effect can be simulated at great cost in CPU cycles.

-Siva

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Tue Aug 31 10:04:27 2004
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy (T & B))
Date: Tue Aug 31 09:57:58 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] MA620/ES620 IrDA works with Nokia Phone!
Message-ID: <4133FFD3.8010209@tandbintl.com>

Dear Friends,

sometimes before, i heard about MA620 (or compatbile ES620) IrDA adapter 
not working or not able to be configured...  I am able to do it with new 
kernel 2.6.8.1. I just want to share with you for our update.

1. Kernel is 2.6.8.1, which is having support for MA600, but it works 
fine for MA620/ES620 also.

2. Ensure that the following modules available and loaded.
    a. uhci_hcd
    b. ircomm-tty
    c. pl2303
    d. ma600-sir
    e. irda
    f. irtty-sir

3. make as script called IrDA_Start.sh with the following content:

#!/bin/sh
#
# Minimal stuff required to get the MA620 USB IrDA dongle recognised by
# the kernel.  Version 1 -- works with unpatched kernel, but only at
# 9600bps.

modprobe uhci_hcd
modprobe pl2303
modprobe irda
**echo 9600 > /proc/sys/net/irda/max_baud_rate
modprobe irtty-sir
modprobe ma600-sir
modprobe ircomm-tty
irattach /dev/usb/ttyUSB0 -d ma600 -s

exit 0

4. I tested it with my Nokia 6610. It works fine. irdadump confirmed it. 
Since I don't have GPRS I can dial into internet but not able to 
connect. That is fine.

5. I used "Kandy phone manager" tool availale in my KDE desktop, which 
works fine with this IrDA, except a few unsupported commands.

Regards
TKSwamy

of the Pentium-M is launched next quarter.

line.  Starting with the dual AMD MP systems 2 years ago, Tiger has
offered server class features (64bit pci, ECC RAM, dual CPU, dual

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Tue Aug 31 10:42:52 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Tue Aug 31 10:42:02 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Utility to shrink fat partition for installing mdk10
References: <20040831045845.62780.qmail@web41109.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <cone.1093929172.289991.326.1000@mynx>

Dhanagopal Rengasamy writes:


> Is there 
> any free utility available to shrink and create
> partition without destroying 
> data?
> 

FIPS 2.0 (http://www.igd.fhg.de/~aschaefe/fips/) should help.
There's also GNU Parted (http://www.gnu.org/software/parted/parted.html) to 
do this. 

NOTE: None of these tools are *guaranteed* against data loss. 
However, I've used FIPS before without losing any data. 

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Tue Aug 31 10:49:39 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)

Chandrashekar Babu writes:


> NOTE: None of these tools are *guaranteed* against data loss. 
> However, I've used FIPS before without losing any data. 

To be a little safe, defragment your FAT partition (using Windows 
utilities) before you get onto resizing it.

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

> 
> Some time ago, I saw a demo of a similar box containing 8 Celeron nodes
> 
 The old VA Linux boxes were along similar lines - now they've moved on
to Itanium 2s after the merger with California Digital - as per 
Anand Babu's talk on the LLNL Thunder.
> 
> I can't believe they chose Transmeta for a HPC box.  Transmeta CPUs have
> a history sacrificing performance for low power consumption.  The VIA
> C3s would have been a better option.  Or wait until the desktop versions
> of the Pentium-M is launched next quarter.
> 
  I agree completely - they could have gone with the Athlon 64 mobiles, or
the Banias, Dothan, Via C3 or PIII mobiles. Transmeta, however, has
an on-chip Northbridge (with Hypertransport on the Efficeon) and very low
power consumption, so it's easier to integrate 12 CPUs on a single board.
Just an engineering tradeoff, but bad from a performance standpoint.
Also the fact that the Orion founder (Colin Hunter) was also a co-founder of
Transmeta seems to have played a role. 

> Just want to add that the Tyan Tiger is an exceptionally good product
> 
  I'd have to agree again, but I haven't played with the Opteron boards.
If somebody has got x86-64 linux running on them with a usable distro,
could they please post their experiences?

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Tue Aug 31 14:18:56 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Tue Aug 31 14:39:01 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] problem in mounting windows partion
In-Reply-To: <20040831085950.97245.qmail@web53705.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20040831084856.E91B632C05@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> [root@localhost naveen]# mount -t vfat /dev/hda2
> /mnt/c
> mount: /dev/hda2 is not a valid block device
> 
1) The entry for /dev/hda2 is missing in /dev. You can
recreate it (as root) with:

mknod /dev/hda2 b 3 2
chgrp disk /dev/hda2

     *or*

2) There isn't a 2nd entry containing a valid partition
in the partition table for /dev/hda. You can create it using
fdisk /dev/hda.

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Tue Aug 31 16:09:59 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Tue Aug 31 16:30:10 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Aproblem in mounting windows partion
In-Reply-To: <F001DE493B12B74BB135AD692FC2BE360F6C84B6@HYDMLVEM01.e2k.ad.ge.com>
Message-ID: <20040831103959.CEDE532C09@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> Recemtly , in linux box, I tried to use "dump2fs" shell comand as root for
> all windows partition, and my system hanged. I rebooted but not able load
> Window anymore..boot loader failed.

I'm guessing that dump2fs (an ext2 fs tool?) destroyed critical
metadata on the windows partitions. Were they NTFS partitions?

> 
> I want to some how recover data from these drives .. any pointer?

If you have some idea of what kind of filesystem (fat16, fat32 or ntfs)
was on the affected partitions, and know their extents (size, start and
end cylinder), there is a fair chance that a windows-based data recovery
tool may be of some help. Your best chances are with FAT16 & FAT32
filesystems.

-Siva

-----Original Message-----
From: ilugc-bounces@ae.iitm.ac.in [mailto:ilugc-bounces@ae.iitm.ac.in]On
Behalf Of Sivasankar Chander
Sent: Tuesday, August 31, 2004 2:19 PM
To: ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in
Cc: Sivasankar Chander
Subject: Re: [Ilugc] problem in mounting windows partion


> [root@localhost naveen]# mount -t vfat /dev/hda2
> /mnt/c
> mount: /dev/hda2 is not a valid block device
> 
1) The entry for /dev/hda2 is missing in /dev. You can
recreate it (as root) with:

mknod /dev/hda2 b 3 2
chgrp disk /dev/hda2

     *or*

2) There isn't a 2nd entry containing a valid partition
in the partition table for /dev/hda. You can create it using
fdisk /dev/hda.

-Siva
